Methods on TargetPolicy\n  // should continue to be called to populate the per-instance configuration.\n  //\n  // Provide an empty `tag` (or call CreatePolicy() with no tag) to create a\n  // policy which never shares its TargetConfig state with another policy\n  // object. For such an object both its TargetConfig and TargetPolicy methods\n  // must be called every time.\n  virtual std::unique_ptr<TargetPolicy> CreatePolicy(std::string_view tag) = 0;\n\n  // Creates a new target (child process) in a suspended state and takes\n  // ownership of |policy|.\n  // Parameters:\n  //   exe_path: This is the full path to the target binary. This parameter\n  //   can be null and in this case the exe path must be the first argument\n  //   of the command_line.\n  //   command_line: The arguments to be passed as command line to the new\n  //   process. This can be null if the exe_path parameter is not null.\n  //   policy: This is the pointer to the policy object for the sandbox to\n  //   be created.\n  //   last_error: If an error or warning is returned from this method this\n  //   parameter will hold the last Win32 error value.\n  //   target: returns the resulting target process information such as process\n  //   handle and PID just as if CreateProcess() had been called. The caller is\n  //   responsible for closing the handles returned in this structure.\n  // Returns:\n  //   ALL_OK if successful. All other return values imply failure.\n  virtual ResultCode SpawnTarget(const wchar_t* exe_path,\n                                 const wchar_t* command_line,\n                                 std::unique_ptr<TargetPolicy> policy,\n                                 DWORD* last_error,\n                                 PROCESS_INFORMATION* target) = 0;\n\n  // Async version of SpawnTarget that supports parallel process launching.\n  // Target creation happens on the thread pool when parallel launching is\n  // enabled (controlled by BrokerServicesDelegate). This function is the same\n  // as SpawnTarget, except the out parameters `last_error`, `target` and\n  // ResultCode are passed to `result_callback`.\n  virtual void SpawnTargetAsync(const wchar_t* exe_path,\n                                const wchar_t* command_line,\n                                std::unique_ptr<TargetPolicy> policy,\n                                SpawnTargetCallback result_callback) = 0;\n\n  // This call creates a snapshot of policies managed by the sandbox and\n  // returns them via a helper class.\n  // Parameters:\n  //   receiver: The |PolicyDiagnosticsReceiver| implementation will be\n  //   called to accept the results of the call.\n  // Returns:\n  //   ALL_OK if the request was dispatched. All other return values\n  //   imply failure, and the responder will not receive its completion\n  //   callback.\n  virtual ResultCode GetPolicyDiagnostics(\n      std::unique_ptr<PolicyDiagnosticsReceiver> receiver) = 0;\n\n  // For the broker, we have some mitigations set early in startup. In\n  // order to properly track those settings, SetStartingMitigations should be\n  // called before other mitigations are set by RatchetDownSecurityMitigations\n  virtual void SetStartingMitigations(MitigationFlags starting_mitigations) = 0;\n\n  // RatchetDownSecurityMitigations is then called by the broker process to\n  // gradually increase our security as startup continues. It's designed to\n  // be called multiple times. If you don't call SetStartingMitigations first\n  // and there were mitigations applied early in startup, the new mitigations\n  // may not be applied.\n  virtual bool RatchetDownSecurityMitigations(\n      MitigationFlags additional_flags) = 0;\n\n protected:\n  ~BrokerServices() {}\n};\n\n// TargetServices models the current process from the perspective\n// of a target process. To obtain a pointer to it use\n// Sandbox::GetTargetServices(). Note that this call returns a non-null\n// pointer only if this process is in fact a target. A process is a target\n// only if the process was spawned by a call to BrokerServices::SpawnTarget().\n//\n// This API allows the target to gain access to resources with a high\n// privilege token and then when it is ready to perform dangerous activities\n// (such as download content from the web) it can lower its token and\n// enter into locked-down (sandbox) mode.\n// The typical usage is as follows:\n//\n//   TargetServices* target_services = Sandbox::GetTargetServices();\n//   if (target_services) {\n//     // We are the target.\n//     target_services->Init();\n//     // Do work that requires high privileges here.\n//     // ....\n//     // When ready to enter lock-down mode call LowerToken:","numLines":200,"startLine":1,"totalLines":312}}}

               // the file system supports.\n  kAllowReadonly,  // Allows open or create with read access only\n                   // (includes access to query the attributes of a file).\n};\n\n// This is the token that\n  //   is used by the process from the creation of the process until the moment\n  //   the process calls TargetServices::LowerToken() or the process calls\n  //   win32's RevertToSelf(). Once this happens the initial token is no longer\n  //   available and the lockdown token is in effect. Using an initial token is\n  //   not compatible with AppContainer, see SetAppContainer.\n  // lockdown: the security level for the token that comes into force after the\n  //   process calls TargetServices::LowerToken() or the process calls\n  //   RevertToSelf(). See the explanation of each level in the TokenLevel\n  //   definition.\n  // Return value: SBOX_ALL_OK if the setting succeeds and false otherwise.\n  //   Returns false if the lockdown value is more permissive than the initial\n  //   value.\n  //\n  // Important: most of the sandbox-provided security relies on this single\n  // setting. The caller should strive to set the lockdown level as restricted\n  // as possible.\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode SetTokenLevel(TokenLevel initial,\n                                                 TokenLevel lockdown) = 0;\n\n  // Returns the initial token level.\n  virtual TokenLevel GetInitialTokenLevel() const = 0;\n\n  // Returns the lockdown token level.\n  virtual TokenLevel GetLockdownTokenLevel() const = 0;\n\n  // Sets the security level of the Job Object to which the target process will\n  // belong. This setting is permanent and cannot be changed once the target\n  // process is spawned. The job controls the global security settings which\n  // can not be specified in the token security profile.\n  // job_level: the security level for the job. See the explanation of each\n  //   level in the JobLevel definition.\n  // ui_exceptions: specify what specific rights that are disabled in the\n  //   chosen job_level that need to be granted. Use this parameter to avoid\n  //   selecting the next permissive job level unless you need all the rights\n  //   that are granted in such level.\n  //   The exceptions can be specified as a combination of the following\n  //   constants:\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_HANDLES : grant access to all user-mode handles. These\n  //   include windows, icons, menus and various GDI objects. In addition the\n  //   target process can set hooks, and broadcast messages to other processes\n  //   that belong to the same desktop.\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_READCLIPBOARD : grant read-only access to the clipboard.\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_WRITECLIPBOARD : grant write access to the clipboard.\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_SYSTEMPARAMETERS : allow changes to the system-wide\n  //   parameters as defined by the Win32 call SystemParametersInfo().\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_DISPLAYSETTINGS : allow programmatic changes to the\n  //  display settings.\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_GLOBALATOMS : allow access to the global atoms table.\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_DESKTOP : allow the creation of new desktops.\n  // JOB_OBJECT_UILIMIT_EXITWINDOWS : allow the call to ExitWindows().\n  //\n  // Return value: SBOX_ALL_OK if the setting succeeds and false otherwise.\n  //\n  // Note: JOB_OBJECT_XXXX constants are defined in winnt.h and documented at\n  // length in:\n  //   http://msdn2.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ms684152.aspx\n  //\n  // Note: the recommended level is JobLevel::kLockdown.\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode SetJobLevel(JobLevel job_level,\n                                               uint32_t ui_exceptions) = 0;\n\n  // Returns the job level.\n  virtual JobLevel GetJobLevel() const = 0;\n\n  // Sets a hard limit on the size of the commit set for the sandboxed process.\n  // If the limit is reached, the process will be terminated with\n  // SBOX_FATAL_MEMORY_EXCEEDED (7012).\n  virtual void SetJobMemoryLimit(size_t memory_limit) = 0;\n\n  // Adds a policy rule effective for processes spawned using this policy.\n  // Files matching `pattern` can be opened following FileSemantics.\n  //\n  // pattern: A specific full path or a full path with wildcard patterns.\n  //   The valid wildcards are:\n  //   '*' : Matches zero or more character. Only one in series allowed.\n  //   '?' : Matches a single character. One or more in series are allowed.\n  // Examples:\n  //   \"c:\\\\documents and settings\\\\vince\\\\*.dmp\"\n  //   \"c:\\\\documents and settings\\\\*\\\\crashdumps\\\\*.dmp\"\n  //   \"c:\\\\temp\\\\app_log_?????_chrome.txt\"\n  //\n  // Note: Do not add new uses of this function - instead proxy file handles\n  // into your process via normal Chrome IPC.\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode AllowFileAccess(FileSemantics semantics,\n                                                   const wchar_t* pattern) = 0;\n\n  // Adds a policy rule effective for processes spawned using this policy.\n  // Modules patching `pattern` (see AllowFileAccess) can still be loaded under\n  // Code-Integrity Guard (MITIGATION_FORCE_MS_SIGNED_BINS).\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode AllowExtraDlls(const wchar_t* pattern) = 0;\n\n  // Adds a policy rule effective for processes spawned using this policy.\n  // Fake gdi init to allow user32 and gdi32 to initialize under Win32 Lockdown.\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode SetFakeGdiInit() = 0;\n\n  // Adds a dll that will be unloaded in the target process before it gets\n  // a chance to initialize itself. The integrity level\n  // will not take effect before you call LowerToken. User Interface Privilege\n  // Isolation is not affected by this setting and will remain off for the\n  // process in the sandbox. If the integrity level is set to a level higher\n  // than the current level, the sandbox will fail to start.\n  virtual void SetDelayedIntegrityLevel(IntegrityLevel level) = 0;\n\n  // Sets the LowBox token for sandboxed process. This is mutually exclusive\n  // with SetAppContainer method.\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode SetLowBox(const wchar_t* sid) = 0;\n\n  // Sets the mitigations enabled when the process is created. Most of these\n  // are implemented as attributes passed via STARTUPINFOEX. So they take\n  // effect before any thread in the target executes. The declaration of\n  // MitigationFlags is followed by a detailed description of each flag.\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode SetProcessMitigations(\n      MitigationFlags flags) = 0;\n\n  // Returns the currently set mitigation flags.\n  virtual MitigationFlags GetProcessMitigations() = 0;\n\n  // Sets process mitigation flags that don't take effect before the call to\n  // LowerToken().\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode SetDelayedProcessMitigations(\n      MitigationFlags flags) = 0;\n\n  // Returns the currently set delayed mitigation flags.\n  virtual MitigationFlags GetDelayedProcessMitigations() const = 0;\n\n  // Adds a restricting random SID to the restricted SIDs list as well as\n  // the default DACL.\n  virtual void AddRestrictingRandomSid() = 0;\n\n  // Locks down the default DACL of the created lockdown and initial tokens\n  // to restrict what other processes are allowed to access a process' kernel\n  // resources.\n  virtual void SetLockdownDefaultDacl() = 0;\n\n  // Configure policy to use an AppContainer profile. |package_name| is the\n  // name of the profile to use.\n  [[nodiscard]] virtual ResultCode AddAppContainerProfile(\n      const wchar_t* package_name) = 0;\n\n  // Get the configured AppContainer. These\n  // are:\n  //  * \"Path\", \"SystemDrive\", \"SystemRoot\", \"TEMP\", \"TMP\": Needed for normal\n  //    operation and tests.\n  //  * \"LOCALAPPDATA\": Needed for App Container processes.\n  //  * \"CHROME_CRASHPAD_PIPE_NAME\": Needed for crashpad.\n  virtual void SetFilterEnvironment(bool filter) = 0;\n\n  // Obtains whether or not the environment for this target should be filtered.\n  // See above for the variables that are allowed.\n  virtual bool GetEnvironmentFiltered() = 0;\n\n  // Zeroes pShimData in the child's PEB.\n  virtual void SetZeroAppShim() = 0;\n};\n\n// We need [[clang::lto_visibility_public]] because instances of this class are\n// passed across module boundaries. These values are mapped to\n// //sandbox/policy/sandbox_type.h values.\nenum Sandbox {\n  // |kService| hosts 'computation only' services such as decoders that\n  // use limited operating system services. Prefer to use this sandbox\n  // if possible.\n  kService,\n\n  // |kServiceWithJit| hosts computation only services that make use of\n  // dynamic code (e.g. v8 or wasm) but do not need access to OS resources.\n  // Prefer |kService| if possible.\n  kServiceWithJit,\n\n  // Hosts generic utilities with limited access to system services.\n  // On some platforms, may be slightly less locked down than |kService|.\n  // For instance, it allows dynamic code and wider access to APIs on Windows.\n  kUtility,\n\n  // The audio service process. May be disabled by policy.\n  kAudio,\n\n  // Hosts the content decryption module. Allows pre-loading of CDM libraries.\n  // - On Windows, when `CdmServiceBroker` is connected the CDM was not\n  // sandboxed to allow CDM preloading.\n  // - On Mac, the process is fully sandboxed when launched.\n  // - On Linux/ChromeOS, the CDM is preloaded in the zygote sandbox.\n  kCdm,\n\n  // The network service. May be disabled by policy.\n  kNetwork,\n\n  // The on-device model execution service. This sandbox is equivalent to the\n  // GPU process's sandbox, but can be used by service processes to host\n  // trustworthy models that may process untrustworthy inputs.\n  kOnDeviceModelExecution,\n\n  // Runs with the same rights as the browser. Usually needed to improve\n  // stability by hosting code that interacts with third party code in another\n  // process.\n  kNoSandbox,\n\n  // Hosts the GPU service and can talk to GPU drivers and other OS APIs which\n  // may not be expecting untrusted input.\n  kGpu,\n\n  // Composits PDF and XPS documents.\n  kPrintCompositor,\n\n  // Hosts untrustworthy web content. Blocks as much OS access as possible.\n  // Unless disabled by policy, allows dynamic code (for wasm/v8). Services\n  // should prefer to use kService or kUtility.\n  kRenderer,\n\n  // Like kUtility but allows loading of speech recognition libraries.\n  kSpeechRecognition,\n\n  // Like kService but allows loading of the optimization guide library.\n  [EnableIf=is_linux]\n  kVideoEffects,\n\n  // Like kUtility but allows loading of screen AI library.\n  [EnableIf=enable_screen_ai_service]\n  kScreenAI,\n\n  // The PPAPI plugin process. This only needs internet access,\n  // policy access, and service access.\n  [EnableIf=is_win]\n  kWindowsSystemProxyResolver,\n\n  // Used to protect processes that perform hardware video decode acceleration.\n  // Currently uses the same policy as the GPU process sandbox. Warm-up does\n  // something different depending on the video acceleration API: for VA-API, we\n  // open the render node and load libva plus associated libraries (like i965 or\n  // iHD). For V4L2, we set up the broker process to allow opening certain V4L2\n  // devices and we load the libv4l2.so library.\n  //\n  // TODO(b/195769334): we're using the GPU process sandbox policy for now as a\n  // transition step. This class inherits from `bpf_dsl::Policy` and serves as the baseline for all other Linux seccomp-BPF policies.
